16 2021-02-25 ear pain The child was administered the vaccine at about 11:15 a.m on 2/7/2021. She woke up about 14 hours la... Read more
Close
The child was administered the vaccine at about 11:15 a.m on 2/7/2021. She woke up about 14 hours later with vaccine side effects the family was prepared for, including headache, chills, nausea, vomiting and fatigue. This all resolved within 48 hours. Approximately one week later, the child woke up again in the night with severe chills in the middle of the night. It was a sudden onset following a week of feeling well. She had to sit in a warm/hot shower for an hour to get warm. She described it as "freezing to death." She has never experienced anything like this before.

Close
Patient was sitting in the observation area. Patient stated that she was feeling "off" and we helped lower her to the ground into a sitting position. She stated that she felt dizzy and we lowered her onto her back and raised her legs onto a chair. 911 was contacted. Patient remained responsive and was able to answer questions throughout. Patient stated that her shoulder felt like it was burning where she received the injection. She also stated that her face felt numb and her lips felt funny (tingling). Patient was still able to breathe and respond appropriately to all questions. Care was taken over by Ambulance service. After speaking with patients mother later in the day, it was determined patient had a vasovagal episode.

16 2021-04-05 tunnel vision Patient is a 16yo seen for her first dose of the COVID-19 vaccine. She was seated in the back seat o... Read more
Close
Patient is a 16yo seen for her first dose of the COVID-19 vaccine. She was seated in the back seat of the car. Shortly after receiving her vaccine (within a few minutes), she chose to move to the front passenger seat of the car, and after sitting in the passenger seat she became lightheaded and lost consciousness. Syncopal event was witnessed and lasted a few seconds. She spontaneously regained consciousness, and complained of some lightheadedness and tunnel vision. No significant confusion was noted, her responses to questions were appropriate. Initial pulse was thready and heart rate initially difficult to auscultate. Pale color noted on the face. Initial pulse approximately 50bpm. Breath sounds clear with good air exchange. Patient was placed in a reclined position with feet on the dash. She quickly recovered and repeat heart rate was auscultated at approximately 70bpm, stronger pulse noted. She was noted to have improvement and she was then driven out of the vaccine site after obtaining consent from her mother (who was the driver) and parked beside EMS. BP was 100/50 and HR 68-72, SaO2 97%. Lightheadedness resolved and she was feeling well, at her baseline. She was monitored for 30 min then allowed to leave with her mother, she was at her baseline at last evaluation. Per history review with her mother, she has had 2 prior episodes of syncope with pin removal from hand after surgery and IV placement.

Kept complaining that she felt like she was crawling in her own skin, all through her arms and her chest, like an itch from the inside. NO HIVES. No difficulty breathing. Kept her home from school and she slept a lot. Only vomited the one time. She was fine by late afternoon and all symptoms seemed to have resolved by then.

16 2021-04-14 double vision, vision blurred Admitted to hospital on 4/10 with 2 day history of mydriasis, diplopia with blurry vision, dizziness... Read more
Close
Admitted to hospital on 4/10 with 2 day history of mydriasis, diplopia with blurry vision, dizziness and balance difficulty. Found to have enhancement of 6th and 3rd CNs on MRI. Patient continued to have blurry and double vision during her stay and mild gait instability. She developed mild frontal headache managed with Tylenol. Her exam was remarkable for mydriasis, mild lateral gaze limitation R>L, mild dysmetria, dizziness and unsteady gait without notable ataxia. No papilledema. Her reflexes were 2+ in her BL UE and LEs. Pediatric Neurology and ophthalmology consulted and followed patient. Eye exam remarkable for bilateral cranial nerve 6 palsy but no other element of CN3 palsy and bilateral dilated but unreactive pupils. Patient treated with IVIG 1mg/kg/day x2 days for likely miller fisher syndrome variant of Guillain-Barre.

16 2021-04-22 lip swelling, eye swelling, ear swelling, mouth swelling Pt. received her second Pfizer dose at 3pm. By 11:30pm she had significant swelling on both of her e... Read more
Close
Pt. received her second Pfizer dose at 3pm. By 11:30pm she had significant swelling on both of her eyes, mouth, and the start of red splotchy skin on arms and legs. We took her to ER. They gave her 50mg of hydroxizine and sent us home. 5min after leaving the ER at 12:30am on 4/23 she felt a golf ball sized lump in her throat and was having difficulty breathing. We brought her back to the ER. At this time they gave her an ekg, and at around 1:30am gave her an epi pin and an oral steroid. Within 5min of the oral steroid and epi pin she no longer had difficulty in breathing and the lump in her throat was gone as was the res splotches. By 5am the swelling in her face had reduced drastically to 90% normal in her left eye and 70% normal in her right eye and 70% normal in her lip. She was released from the ER at 5:45am and went home to sleep. At 11:30am on 4/23 her swelling in her face remains the same and she is complaining of a headache. She was given 50mg more of hydroxizine.

Patient had not recovered from the events, at the time of the report.; Sender's Comments: The events left neck pain, and then progressed to left facial drooping, loss of taste on anterior part of tongue, and decreased tear production in her left eye are considered possibly related to the suspect product based on temporal association. The impact of this report on the benefit/risk profile of the Pfizer product is evaluated as part of Pfizer procedures for safety evaluation, including the review and analysis of aggregate data for adverse events. Close
I made sure to hydrate and eat well the day of the vaccine. I have had no allergic reactions to any medications/ injections in the past and I was not worried about this one. I didn't take any meds beforehand besides my normal morning modafinil. I have no fear of needles. I received the vaccine in the auditorium about 1:25pm. The RN did a fantastic job, went through all of the information, no pain at all with the injection. As I was sitting in my chair for monitoring, a few minutes in I began to feel very uncomfortable. I felt clammy/sweaty and kept shifting my weight in my seat. I didn't want to make a big deal of it at first because I worried it was all in my head. But I became more and more uncomfortable. I laid my head down on the little desk, no help. I closed my eyes, no help. About 10 minutes or so in I decided to ask if they had water available. I slowly got up and walked to the back of the room. I couldn't even get the question out of my mouth before the nurse told me to sit down. Apparently I was white as a ghost. They got a wheelchair and wheeled me to the space behind the auditorium. By then I was starting to feel like my throat was closing and I saw spots in my peripheral vision. It was kind of a blur from there. I tried to take deep breaths. I drank a few sips of water and poured some on a paper towel to wet my forehead (and spilled all over my lap because I was a little disoriented at this point). My BP was 60s/40s and then 60s/30s. A rapid response was called. They moved me to a cart flat on my back with my legs elevated. My fingers and toes were starting to go numb and my lips were apparently blue/ white. After laying for a few minutes in Trendelenburg my BP began to resolve and my breathing started to ease a bit. No further intervention was done by the rapid team. I was taken by the Rapid RN to the ED for monitoring. They eventually pushed the cart into a room and took some vitals and an EKG. They had me stand and move to a wheelchair. I felt horrible but improved from before. They had me sit in a wheelchair in the lobby for a few hours before taking me back and placing an IV and drawing labs (I believe it was 3 hours from the initial reaction). I gave a urine sample. They then put me in a wheelchair and wheeled me back into the lobby for some more time. Then, they wheeled me back to a room where they gave some lactated ringers and a PA and MD saw me. By then my BP and breathing was completely resolved. The MD said he wasn't fully convinced it was just a vasovagal episode because I haven't had issues with vaccines in the past and I was well hydrated and my HR was normal. It partly fit the picture for an allergic reaction/ severe immune response d/t the feeling of throat closing, the BP drop, and the elevated WBCs. They advised that I list the vaccine as an allergy and do not get the second dose, especially since I had COVID back in September.
